migrate to type hints instead\n   229→- **No trailing whitespace**: Always clean up trailing spaces on lines, especially when editing existing files\n   230→\n   231→### Python Version Support\n   232→\n   233→- Controller code: support range defined in `pyproject.toml`\n   234→- Modules/module_utils: minimum version in `lib/ansible/module_utils/basic.py` (`_PY_MIN`) up to max from `pyproject.toml`\n   235→- Modules support a wider Python version range than controller code\n   236→\n   237→### Dependencies and Imports\n   238→\n   239→- Prefer Python stdlib over external dependencies\n   240→- Use existing code from within the Ansible project\n   241→- `lib/ansible/modules/` can only import from `lib/ansible/module_utils/` (modules are packaged for remote execution)\n   242→- `lib/ansible/module_utils/` cannot import from outside itself\n   243→\n   244→## Documentation Standards\n   245→\n   246→### Module and Plugin Documentation\n   247→\n   248→- Modules and plugins require DOCUMENTATION, EXAMPLES, and RETURN blocks as static YAML string variables\n   249→- These blocks cannot be dynamically generated - they are parsed via AST/token parsing\n   250→- Alternative: \"sidecar\" documentation as `.yml` files with same stem name adjacent to plugin files\n   251→- All modules should have a `main()` function and `if __name__ == '__main__':` block\n   252→- Use `version_added` fields in documentation following existing version format patterns\n   253→\n   254→### Changelog Requirements\n   255→\n   256→- Changes require entries in `changelogs/fragments/` as YAML files\n   257→- Create a new fragment file per PR (never reuse existing fragments to avoid merge conflicts)\n   258→- Fragment structure follows sections defined in `changelogs/config.yaml` under the `sections` key\n   259→- Naming: `{issue_number}-{short-description}.yml` or `{component}-{description}.yml` if no issue\n   260→- Format: `- {component} - {description} ({optional URL to GH issue})`\n   261→- Content supports Sphinx markup (use double backticks for code references)\n   262→\n   263→## Repository Management\n   264→\n   265→### Plugin Development\n   266→\n   267→- New plugins should go into collections, not ansible-core\n   268→- ansible-core rarely accepts new plugins; core team makes these decisions\n   269→\n   270→### Branch and Release Management\n   271→\n   272→- All PRs target the `devel` branch\n   273→- Use GitHub templates when creating issues/PRs (`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/` and `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE/`)\n   274→- For issues: fill out the `component` field with project root relative file path\n   275→- For PRs: adjust the issue type in the template as listed in `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n   276→- Validate issues are fixed in `devel` before reporting against stable releases\n   277→- Bug fixes: backported to latest stable only\n   278→- Critical bug fixes: backported to latest and previous stable\n   279→- Security issues: contact security@ansible.com privately, not via GitHub\n   280→\n   281→### Backwards Compatibility\n   282→\n   283→- Backwards compatibility is prioritized over most other concerns\n   284→- Deprecation cycle: 4 releases (deprecation + 2 releases + removal)\n   285→- Use `Display.deprecated` or `AnsibleModule.deprecate` with version from `lib/ansible/release.py` plus 3\n   286→- Example: deprecating in 2.19 means removal in 2.22\n   287→\n   288→## Code Structure Reference\n   289→\n   290→### Core Structure\n   291→\n   292→- `lib/ansible/` - Main Ansible library code\n   293→  - `cli/` - Command-line interface implementations (ansible, ansible-playbook, etc.)\n   294→  - `executor/` - Task execution engine and strategies (includes PowerShell support in `powershell/`)\n   295→  - `inventory/` - Inventory management and parsing\n   296→  - `modules/` - Core modules (built-in automation modules)\n   297→  - `module_utils/` - Shared utilities for modules (includes C# in `csharp/` and PowerShell in `powershell/`)\n   298→  - `plugins/` - Plugin framework (filters, tests, lookups, etc.)\n   299→  - `vars/` - Variable management\n   300→  - `config/` - Configuration handling\n   301→  - `collections/` - Ansible Collections framework\n   302→\n   303→### Key Components\n   304→\n   305→- **CLI Layer**: Entry points in `lib/ansible/cli/` handle command parsing and dispatch\n   306→- **Executor**: `lib/ansible/executor/` contains the core execution engine that runs tasks and plays\n   307→- **Module System**: Modules in `lib/ansible/modules/` are the units of work; they're executed remotely\n   308→- **Plugin Architecture**: `lib/ansible/plugins/` provides extensibility through filters, tests, lookups, etc.\n   309→- **Inventory**: `lib/ansible/inventory/` manages host and group definitions\n   310→- **Collections**: Modern packaging format for distributing Ansible content\n   311→\n   312→### Testing Infrastructure\n   313→\n   314→- `test/units/` - Unit tests mirroring the lib structure\n   315→- `test/integration/` - Integration tests organized by target (named after plugin/functionality being tested)\n   316→  - Some targets have `context/controller` or `context/target` in their `aliases` file when not easily inferable\n   317→  - Only modules run on target hosts; all other plugins execute locally in the ansible process\n   318→- `test/lib/` - Test utilities and frameworks\n   319→- `ansible-test` - Unified testing tool for all test types\n   320→\n   321→For CI failure debugging, see [Helping Developers with CI Failures](#helping-developers-with-ci-failures).\n   322→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Common CI failure patterns:**\n\n- **Sanity failures**: Usually have specific fixes (trailing whitespace, import errors, etc.)\n- **Integration test failures**: May require platform-specific containers or test adjustments\n- **Unit test failures**: Often indicate actual code issues that need debugging\n\n**4. For test failures, run the same tests locally using `ansible-test` to reproduce and debug\n\n## PR Review Guidelines\n\n### PR Review Checklist\n\nUse this checklist for EVERY PR review:\n\n```text\n□ Created TodoWrite list for review steps\n□ Step 1: Get PR details with gh pr view <number>\n□ Step 2: Get PR diff with gh pr diff <number>\n□ Step 3: Check required components (changelog, tests)\n□ Step 4: Checkout PR branch with gh pr checkout <number>\n□ Step 5: Review existing feedback with gh pr view <number> --comments\n□ Step 6: Verify all issues addressed\n□ Step 7: Call out any unresolved feedback\n□ Mark each TodoWrite item as completed when done\n```\n\nWhen assisting with PR reviews, verify:\n\n### Required Components\n\n- Changelog fragment exists in `changelogs/fragments/`\n- Appropriate tests are included and cover the changed code\n  - Unit tests should be pytest style, and functional rather than tightly coupled to mocking\n  - Integration tests required for almost all plugin changes (tests the public API)\n  - Tests should exercise the actual changed code, not just add random coverage\n\n### Review Process\n\nFollow these steps in order for thorough PR reviews:\n\n1. **Get PR details**: Use `gh pr view <number>` to understand the PR scope and description\n2. **Get PR diff**: Use `gh pr diff <number>` to see all changes\n3. **Check required components FIRST**:\n   - Verify changelog fragment exists and uses correct section (check `changelogs/config.yaml` for valid sections)\n   - Verify tests exist and specifically cover the changed code paths\n4. **Checkout PR branch**: Use `gh pr checkout <number>` to examine code holistically with changes applied\n5. **Review existing feedback**: Use `gh pr view <number> --comments` to see all comments and previous review feedback\n6. **Verify all issues addressed**: Ensure all bot failures, reviewer requests, and discussion points are resolved\n7. **Call out any unresolved review feedback**: Explicitly mention any discussions or requests that remain unaddressed\n\n### Common Review Issues to Check\n\n- **Changelog section errors**: Verify changelog uses valid section from `changelogs/config.yaml`. Fragment structure follows sections defined there.\n- **Test scope**: Ensure tests exercise the actual changed code, not just add random coverage.\n  Integration tests required for almost all plugin changes (tests the public API).\n  Tests should be functional rather than tightly coupled to mocking.\n\n### Review Task Management\n\n- Use TodoWrite tool to track review steps for complex PRs\n- Mark tasks as in_progress when actively working on them\n- Complete tasks immediately after finishing each step\n- This provides visibility to users about review progress\n\n### Review Tools\n\n- `gh pr view <number>` - Get PR details and description\n- `gh pr view <number> --comments` - See all comments and review feedback\n- `gh pr diff <number>` - Get complete diff of changes\n- `gh pr checkout <number>` - Switch to PR branch for holistic examination\n- `Read` tool - Examine specific changed files in detail\n- `Grep` tool - Search for related code patterns or test coverage (uses ripgrep/rg)\n\n## Development Guidelines\n\n### Code Style Notes\n\n- Line limit is 160 characters (not 80)\n- E402 (module level import not at top) is ignored\n- In `lib/ansible/modules/`, imports must come after DOCUMENTATION, EXAMPLES, and RETURN definitions\n- Don't add obvious comments about code\n- Use native type hints with `from __future__ import annotations` (converts to strings at runtime)\n- Don't document module parameters in docstrings - migrate to type hints instead\n- **No trailing whitespace**: Always clean up trailing spaces on lines, especially when editing existing files\n\n### Python Version Support\n\n- Controller code: support range defined in `pyproject.toml`\n- Modules/module_utils: minimum version in `lib/ansible/module_utils/basic.py` (`_PY_MIN`) up to max from `pyproject.toml`\n- Modules support a wider Python version range than controller code\n\n### Dependencies and Imports\n\n- Prefer Python stdlib over external dependencies\n- Use existing code from within the Ansible project\n- `lib/ansible/modules/` can only import from `lib/ansible/module_utils/` (modules are packaged for remote execution)\n- `lib/ansible/module_utils/` cannot import from outside itself\n\n## Documentation Standards\n\n### Module and Plugin Documentation\n\n- Modules and plugins require DOCUMENTATION, EXAMPLES, and RETURN blocks as static YAML string variables\n- These blocks cannot be dynamically generated - they are parsed via AST/token parsing\n- Alternative: \"sidecar\" documentation as `.yml` files with same stem name adjacent to plugin files\n- All modules should have a `main()` function and `if __name__ == '__main__':` block\n- Use `version_added` fields in documentation following existing version format patterns\n\n### Changelog Requirements\n\n- Changes require entries in `changelogs/fragments/` as YAML files\n- Create a new fragment file per PR (never reuse existing fragments to avoid merge conflicts)\n- Fragment structure follows sections defined in `changelogs/config.yaml` under the `sections` key\n- Naming: `{issue_number}-{short-description}.yml` or `{component}-{description}.yml` if no issue\n- Format: `- {component} - {description} ({optional URL to GH issue})`\n- Content supports Sphinx markup (use double backticks for code references)\n\n## Repository Management\n\n### Plugin Development\n\n- New plugins should go into collections, not ansible-core\n- ansible-core rarely accepts new plugins; core team makes these decisions\n\n### Branch and Release Management\n\n- All PRs target the `devel` branch\n- Use GitHub templates when creating issues/PRs (`.github/ISSUE_TEMPLATE/` and `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE/`)\n- For issues: fill out the `component` field with project root relative file path\n- For PRs: adjust the issue type in the template as listed in `.github/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE/PULL_REQUEST_TEMPLATE.md`\n- Validate issues are fixed in `devel` before reporting against stable releases\n- Bug fixes: backported to latest stable only\n- Critical bug fixes: backported to latest and previous stable\n- Security issues: contact security@ansible.com privately, not via GitHub\n\n### Backwards Compatibility\n\n- Backwards compatibility is prioritized over most other concerns\n- Deprecation cycle: 4 releases (deprecation + 2 releases + removal)\n- Use `Display.deprecated` or `AnsibleModule.deprecate` with version from `lib/ansible/release.py` plus 3\n- Example: deprecating in 2.19 means removal in 2.22\n\n## Code Structure Reference\n\n### Core Structure\n\n- `lib/ansible/` - Main Ansible library code\n  - `cli/` - Command-line interface implementations (ansible, ansible-playbook, etc.)\n  - `executor/` - Task execution engine and strategies (includes PowerShell support in `powershell/`)\n  - `inventory/` - Inventory management and parsing\n  - `modules/` - Core modules (built-in automation modules)\n  - `module_utils/` - Shared utilities for modules (includes C# in `csharp/` and PowerShell in `powershell/`)\n  - `plugins/` - Plugin framework (filters, tests, lookups, etc.)\n  - `vars/` - Variable management\n  - `config/` - Configuration handling\n  - `collections/` - Ansible Collections framework\n\n### Key Components\n\n- **CLI Layer**: Entry points in `lib/ansible/cli/` handle command parsing and dispatch\n- **Executor**: `lib/ansible/executor/` contains the core execution engine that runs tasks and plays\n- **Module System**: Modules in `lib/ansible/modules/` are the units of work; they're executed remotely\n- **Plugin Architecture**: `lib/ansible/plugins/` provides extensibility through filters, tests, lookups, etc.\n- **Inventory**: `lib/ansible/inventory/` manages host and group definitions\n- **Collections**: Modern packaging format for distributing Ansible content\n\n### Testing Infrastructure\n\n- `test/units/` - Unit tests mirroring the lib structure\n- `test/integration/` - Integration tests organized by target (named after plugin/functionality being tested)\n  - Some targets have `context/controller` or `context/target` in their `aliases` file when not easily inferable\n  - Only modules run on target hosts; all other plugins execute locally in the ansible process\n- `test/lib/` - Test utilities and frameworks\n- `ansible-test` - Unified testing tool for all test types\n\nFor CI failure debugging, see [Helping Developers with CI Failures](#helping-developers-with-ci-failures).\n","numLines":322,"startLine":1,"totalLines":322}}}

restrict access to ansible files that exist\n\n                return None  # ansible file does not exist, do not restrict access\n\n            if is_name_in_namepace(fullname, ['ansible_collections']):\n                if not collection_loader:\n                    return self  # restrict access to collections when we are not testing a collection\n\n                if not self.restrict_to_module_paths:\n                    return None  # for non-modules, everything in the ansible namespace is allowed\n\n                if is_name_in_namepace(fullname, ['ansible_collections...plugins.module_utils', self.name]):\n                    return None  # module_utils and module under test are always allowed\n\n                if collection_loader.find_module(fullname, path):\n                    return self  # restrict access to collection files that exist\n\n                return None  # collection file does not exist, do not restrict access\n\n            # not a namespace we care about\n            return None\n\n        def create_module(self, spec):  # pylint: disable=unused-argument\n            # type: (RestrictedModuleLoader, ModuleSpec) -> None\n            \"\"\"Return None to use default module creation.\"\"\"\n            return None\n\n        def exec_module(self, module):\n            # type: (RestrictedModuleLoader, types.ModuleType) -> None | ImportError\n            \"\"\"Execute the module if the name is ansible.module_utils.basic and otherwise raise an ImportError\"\"\"\n            fullname = module.__spec__.name\n            if fullname == 'ansible.module_utils.basic':\n                self.loaded_modules.add(fullname)\n                for path in convert_ansible_name_to_absolute_paths(fullname):\n                    if not os.path.exists(path):\n                        continue\n                    loader = SourceFileLoader(fullname, path)\n                    spec = spec_from_loader(fullname, loader)\n                    real_module = module_from_spec(spec)\n                    loader.exec_module(real_module)\n                    real_module.AnsibleModule = ImporterAnsibleModule  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n                    real_module._load_params = lambda *args, **kwargs: {}  # type: ignore[attr-defined] # pylint: disable=protected-access\n                    sys.modules[fullname] = real_module\n                    return None\n                raise ImportError('could not find \"%s\"' % fullname)\n            raise ImportError('import of \"%s\" is not allowed in this context' % fullname)\n\n        def load_module(self, fullname):\n            # type: (RestrictedModuleLoader, str) -> types.ModuleType | ImportError\n            \"\"\"Return the module if the name is ansible.module_utils.basic and otherwise raise an ImportError.\"\"\"\n            if fullname == 'ansible.module_utils.basic':\n                module = self.__load_module(fullname)\n\n                # stop Ansible module execution during AnsibleModule instantiation\n                module.AnsibleModule = ImporterAnsibleModule  # type: ignore[attr-defined]\n                # no-op for _load_params since it may be called before instantiating AnsibleModule\n                module._load_params = lambda *args, **kwargs: {}  # type: ignore[attr-defined] # pylint: disable=protected-access\n\n                return module\n\n            raise ImportError('import of \"%s\" is not allowed in this context' % fullname)\n\n        def __load_module(self, fullname):\n            # type: (RestrictedModuleLoader, str) -> types.ModuleType\n            \"\"\"Load the requested module while avoiding infinite recursion.\"\"\"\n            self.loaded_modules.add(fullname)\n            return import_module(fullname)\n\n    def run(restrict_to_module_paths):\n        \"\"\"Main program function.\"\"\"\n        base_dir = os.getcwd()\n        messages = set()\n\n        for path in sys.argv[1:] or sys.stdin.read().splitlines():\n            name = convert_relative_path_to_name(path)\n            test_python_module(path, name, base_dir, messages, restrict_to_module_paths)\n\n        if messages:\n            sys.exit(10)\n\n    def test_python_module(path, name, base_dir, messages, restrict_to_module_paths):\n        \"\"\"Test the given python module by importing it.\n        :type path: str\n        :type name: str\n        :type base_dir: str\n        :type messages: set[str]\n        :type restrict_to_module_paths: bool\n        \"\"\"\n        if name in sys.modules:\n            return  # cannot be tested because it has already been loaded\n\n        is_ansible_module = (path.startswith('lib/ansible/modules/') or path.startswith('plugins/modules/')) and os.path.basename(path) != '__init__.py'\n        run_main = is_ansible_module\n\n        if path == 'lib/ansible/modules/async_wrapper.py':\n            # async_wrapper is a non-standard Ansible module (does not use AnsibleModule) so we cannot test the main function\n            run_main = False\n\n        capture_normal = Capture()\n        capture_main = Capture()\n\n        run_module_ok = False\n\n        try:\n            with monitor_sys_modules(path, messages):\n                with restrict_imports(path, name, messages, restrict_to_module_paths):\n                    with capture_output(capture_normal):\n                        import_module(name)\n\n            if run_main:\n                run_module_ok = is_ansible_module\n\n                with monitor_sys_modules(path, messages):\n                    with restrict_imports(path, name, messages, restrict_to_module_paths):\n                        with capture_output(capture_main):\n                            runpy.run_module(name, run_name='__main__', alter_sys=True)\n        except ImporterAnsibleModuleException:\n            # module instantiated AnsibleModule without raising an exception\n            if not run_module_ok:\n                if is_ansible_module:\n                    report_message(path, 0, 0, 'module-guard', \"AnsibleModule instantiation not guarded by `if __name__ == '__main__'`\", messages)\n                else:\n                    report_message(path, 0, 0, 'non-module', \"AnsibleModule instantiated by import of non-module\", messages)\n        except BaseException as ex:  # pylint: disable=locally-disabled, broad-except\n            # intentionally catch all exceptions, including calls to sys.exit\n            exc_type, _exc, exc_tb = sys.exc_info()\n            message = str(ex)\n            results = list(reversed(traceback.extract_tb(exc_tb)))\n            line = 0\n            offset = 0\n            full_path = os.path.join(base_dir, path)\n            base_path = base_dir + os.path.sep\n            source = None\n\n            # avoid line wraps in messages\n            message = re.sub(r'\\n *', ': ', message)\n\n            for result in results:\n                if result[0] == full_path:\n                    # save the line number for the file under test\n                    line = result[1] or 0\n\n                if not source and result[0].startswith(base_path) and not result[0].startswith(temp_path):\n                    # save the first path and line number in the traceback which is in our source tree\n                    source = (os.path.relpath(result[0], base_path), result[1] or 0, 0)\n\n            if isinstance(ex, SyntaxError):\n                # SyntaxError has better information than the traceback\n                if ex.filename == full_path:  # pylint: disable=locally-disabled, no-member\n                    # syntax error was reported in the file under test\n                    line = ex.lineno or 0  # pylint: disable=locally-disabled, no-member\n                    offset = ex.offset or 0  # pylint: disable=locally-disabled, no-member\n                elif ex.filename.startswith(base_path) and not ex.filename.startswith(temp_path):  # pylint: disable=locally-disabled, no-member\n                    # syntax error was reported in our source tree\n                    source = (os.path.relpath(ex.filename, base_path), ex.lineno or 0, ex.offset or 0)  # pylint: disable=locally-disabled, no-member\n\n                # remove the filename and line number from the message\n                # either it was extracted above, or it's not really useful information\n                message = re.sub(r' \\(.*?, line [0-9]+\\)$', '', message)\n\n            if source and source[0] != path:\n                message += ' (at %s:%d:%d)' % (source[0], source[1], source[2])\n\n            report_message(path, line, offset, 'traceback', '%s: %s' % (exc_type.__name__, message), messages)\n        finally:\n            capture_report(path, capture_normal, messages)\n            capture_report(path, capture_main, messages)\n\n    def is_name_in_namepace(name, namespaces):\n        \"\"\"Returns True if the given name is one of the given namespaces, otherwise returns False.\"\"\"\n        name_parts = name.split('.')\n\n        for namespace in namespaces:\n            namespace_parts = namespace.split('.')\n            length = min(len(name_parts), len(namespace_parts))\n\n            truncated_name = name_parts[0:length]\n            truncated_namespace = namespace_parts[0:length]\n\n            # empty parts in the namespace are treated as wildcards\n            # to simplify the comparison, use those empty parts to indicate the positions in the name to be empty as well\n            for idx, part in enumerate(truncated_namespace):\n                if not part:\n                    truncated_name[idx] = part\n\n            # example: name=ansible, allowed_name=ansible.module_utils\n            # example: name=ansible.module_utils.system.ping, allowed_name=ansible.module_utils\n            if truncated_name == truncated_namespace:\n                return True\n\n        return False\n\n    def check_sys_modules(path, before, messages):\n        \"\"\"Check for unwanted changes to sys.modules.\n        :type path: str\n        :type before: dict[str, module]\n        :type messages: set[str]\n        \"\"\"\n        after = sys.modules\n        removed = set(before.keys()) - set(after.keys())\n        changed = set(key for key, value in before.items() if key in after and value != after[key])\n\n        # additions are checked by our custom PEP 302 loader, so we don't need to check them again here\n\n        for module in sorted(removed):\n            report_message(path, 0, 0, 'unload', 'unloading of \"%s\" in sys.modules is not supported' % module, messages)\n\n        for module in sorted(changed):\n            report_message(path, 0, 0, 'reload', 'reloading of \"%s\" in sys.modules is not supported' % module, messages)\n\n    def convert_ansible_name_to_absolute_paths(name):\n        \"\"\"Calculate the module path from the given name.\n        :type name: str\n        :rtype: list[str]\n        \"\"\"\n        return [\n            os.path.join(ansible_path, name.replace('.', os.path.sep)),\n            os.path.join(ansible_path, name.replace('.', os.path.sep)) + '.py',\n        ]\n\n    def convert_relative_path_to_name(path):\n        \"\"\"Calculate the module name from the given path.\n        :type path: str\n        :rtype: str\n        \"\"\"\n        if path.endswith('/__init__.py'):\n            clean_path = os.path.dirname(path)\n        else:\n            clean_path = path\n\n        clean_path = os.path.splitext(clean_path)[0]\n\n        name = clean_path.replace(os.path.sep, '.')\n\n        if collection_loader:\n            # when testing collections the relative paths (and names) being tested are within the collection under test\n            name = 'ansible_collections.%s.%s' % (collection_full_name, name)\n        else:\n            # when testing ansible all files being imported reside under the lib directory\n            name = name[len('lib/'):]\n\n        return name\n\n    class Capture:\n        \"\"\"Captured output and/or exception.\"\"\"\n\n        def __init__(self):\n            # use buffered IO to simulate StringIO; allows Ansible's stream patching to behave without warnings\n            self.stdout = TextIOWrapper(BytesIO())\n            self.stderr = TextIOWrapper(BytesIO())\n\n    def capture_report(path, capture, messages):\n        \"\"\"Report on captured output.\n        :type path: str\n        :type capture: Capture\n        :type messages: set[str]\n        \"\"\"\n        # since we're using buffered IO, flush before checking for data\n        capture.stdout.flush()\n        capture.stderr.flush()\n        stdout_value = capture.stdout.buffer.getvalue()\n        if stdout_value:\n            first = stdout_value.decode().strip().splitlines()[0].strip()\n            report_message(path, 0, 0, 'stdout', first, messages)\n\n        stderr_value = capture.stderr.buffer.getvalue()\n        if stderr_value:\n            first = stderr_value.decode().strip().splitlines()[0].strip()\n            report_message(path, 0, 0, 'stderr', first, messages)\n\n    def report_message(path, line, column, code, message, messages):\n        \"\"\"Report message if not already reported.\n        :type path: str\n        :type line: int\n        :type column: int\n        :type code: str\n        :type message: str\n        :type messages: set[str]\n        \"\"\"\n        message = '%s:%d:%d: %s: %s' % (path, line, column, code, message)\n\n        if message not in messages:\n            messages.add(message)\n            print(message)\n\n    @contextlib.contextmanager\n    def restrict_imports(path, name, messages, restrict_to_module_paths):\n        \"\"\"Restrict available imports.\n        :type path: str\n        :type name: str\n        :type messages: set[str]\n        :type restrict_to_module_paths: bool\n        \"\"\"\n        restricted_loader = RestrictedModuleLoader(path, name, restrict_to_module_paths)\n\n        # noinspection PyTypeChecker\n        sys.meta_path.insert(0, restricted_loader)\n        sys.path_importer_cache.clear()\n\n        try:\n            yield\n        finally:\n            if import_type == 'plugin' and not collection_loader:\n                from ansible.utils.collection_loader._collection_finder import _AnsibleCollectionFinder\n\n                _AnsibleCollectionFinder._remove()  # pylint: disable=protected-access\n\n            if sys.meta_path[0] != restricted_loader:\n                report_message(path, 0, 0, 'metapath', 'changes to sys.meta_path[0] are not permitted', messages)\n\n            while restricted_loader in sys.meta_path:\n                # noinspection PyTypeChecker\n                sys.meta_path.remove(restricted_loader)\n\n            sys.path_importer_cache.clear()\n\n    @contextlib.contextmanager\n    def monitor_sys_modules(path, messages):\n        \"\"\"Monitor sys.modules for unwanted changes, reverting any additions made to our own namespaces.\"\"\"\n        snapshot = sys.modules.copy()\n\n        try:\n            yield\n        finally:\n            check_sys_modules(path, snapshot, messages)\n\n            for key in set(sys.modules.keys()) - set(snapshot.keys()):\n                if is_name_in_namepace(key, ('ansible', 'ansible_collections')):\n                    del sys.modules[key]  # only unload our own code since we know it's native Python\n\n    @contextlib.contextmanager\n    def capture_output(capture):\n        \"\"\"Capture sys.stdout and sys.stderr.\n        :type capture: Capture\n        \"\"\"\n        old_stdout = sys.stdout\n        old_stderr = sys.stderr\n\n        sys.stdout = capture.stdout\n        sys.stderr = capture.stderr\n\n        # clear all warnings registries to make all warnings available\n        for module in sys.modules.values():\n            try:\n                # noinspection PyUnresolvedReferences\n                module.__warningregistry__.clear()\n            except AttributeError:\n                pass\n\n        with warnings.catch_warnings():\n            warnings.simplefilter('error')\n\n            if collection_loader and import_type == 'plugin':\n                warnings.filterwarnings(\n                    \"ignore\",\n                    \"AnsibleCollectionFinder has already been configured\")\n\n            try:\n                yield\n            finally:\n                sys.stdout = old_stdout\n                sys.stderr = old_stderr\n\n    run(import_type == 'module')\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    main()\n","numLines":560,"startLine":1,"totalLines":560}}}

self.alternative = alternative\n        self.modules_only = modules_only\n        self.names = set(names) if names else set()\n        self.ignore_paths = ignore_paths\n        self.ansible_test_only = ansible_test_only\n\n    def applies_to(self, path, name=None):  # type: (str, t.Optional[str]) -> bool\n        \"\"\"Return True if this entry applies to the given path, otherwise return False.\"\"\"\n        if self.names:\n            if not name:\n                return False\n\n            if name not in self.names:\n                return False\n\n        if self.ignore_paths and any(path.endswith(ignore_path) for ignore_path in self.ignore_paths):\n            return False\n\n        if self.ansible_test_only and '/test/lib/ansible_test/_internal/' not in path:\n            return False\n\n        if self.modules_only:\n            return is_module_path(path)\n\n        return True\n\n\ndef is_module_path(path):  # type: (str) -> bool\n    \"\"\"Return True if the given path is a module or module_utils path, otherwise return False.\"\"\"\n    return path.startswith(ANSIBLE_TEST_MODULES_PATH) or path.startswith(ANSIBLE_TEST_MODULE_UTILS_PATH)\n\n\nclass 'ansible-bad-import-from'\n    BAD_FUNCTION = 'ansible-bad-function'\n    BAD_MODULE_IMPORT = 'ansible-bad-module-import'\n\n    msgs = dict(\n        E5101=('Import %s instead of %s',\n astroid.nodes.Import) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Visit an import node.\"\"\"\n        for name in node.names:\n            self._check_import(node, name[0])\n\n    def visit_importfrom(self, node: astroid.nodes.ImportFrom) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Visit an import from node.\"\"\"\n        self._check_importfrom(node, node.modname, node.names)\n\n    def visit_attribute(self, node: astroid.nodes.Attribute) -> None:\n        \"\"\"Visit an attribute node.\"\"\"\n        last_child = node.last_child()\n\n        # this is faster than using type inference and will catch the most common cases\n        if not isinstance(last_child, astroid.nodes.Name):\n            return\n\n        module = last_child.name\n\n        entry = self.unwanted_imports.get(module)\n\n        if func = None\n\n                if isinstance(i.parent, astroid.nodes.Module):\n                    parent_module = i.parent.name\n                elif isinstance(i.parent, astroid.nodes.If) and isinstance(i.parent.parent, astroid.nodes.Module):\n                    parent_module = i.parent.parent.name\n                else:\n                    parent_module = None\n\n                if parent_module == 'posix':\n                    parent_module = 'os'  # some os.* functions we're looking for show up as posix.* imports\n\n                if parent_module and isinstance(i, (astroid.nodes.FunctionDef, astroid.nodes.ClassDef)):\n                    func = f'{parent_module}.{i.name}'\n\n                if not func:\n                    continue\n\n                entry = {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"type":"text","text":"# Simplify: Code Review and Cleanup\n\nReview all changed files for reuse, quality, and efficiency. Fix any issues found.\n\n## Phase 1: Identify Changes\n\nRun `git diff` (or `git diff HEAD` if there are staged changes) to see what changed. If there are no git changes, review the most recently modified files that the user mentioned or that you edited earlier in this conversation.\n\n## Phase 2: Launch Three Review Agents in Parallel\n\nUse the Agent tool to launch all three agents concurrently in a single message. Pass each agent the full diff so it has the complete context.\n\n### Agent 1: Code Reuse Review\n\nFor each change:\n\n1. **Search for existing utilities and helpers** that could replace newly written code. Use Grep to find similar patterns elsewhere in the codebase — common locations are utility directories, shared modules, and files adjacent to the changed ones.\n2. **Flag any new function that duplicates existing functionality.** Suggest the existing function to use instead.\n3. **Flag any inline logic that could use an existing utility** — hand-rolled string manipulation, manual path handling, custom environment checks, ad-hoc type guards, and similar patterns are common candidates.\n\n### Agent 2: Code Quality Review\n\nReview the same changes for hacky patterns:\n\n1. **Redundant state**: state that duplicates existing state, cached values that could be derived, observers/effects that could be direct calls\n2. **Parameter sprawl**: adding new parameters to a function instead of generalizing or restructuring existing ones\n3. **Copy-paste with slight variation**: near-duplicate code blocks that should be unified with a shared abstraction\n4. **Leaky abstractions**: exposing internal details that should be encapsulated, or breaking existing abstraction boundaries\n5. **Stringly-typed code**: using raw strings where constants, enums (string unions), or branded types already exist in the codebase\n\n### Agent 3: Efficiency Review\n\nReview the same changes for efficiency:\n\n1. **Unnecessary work**: redundant computations, repeated file reads, duplicate network/API calls, N+1 patterns\n2. **Missed concurrency**: independent operations run sequentially when they could run in parallel\n3. **Hot-path bloat**: new blocking work added to startup or per-request/per-render hot paths\n4. **Unnecessary existence checks**: pre-checking file/resource existence before operating (TOCTOU anti-pattern) — operate directly and handle the error\n5. **Memory**: unbounded data structures, missing cleanup, event listener leaks\n6. **Overly broad operations**: reading entire files when only a portion is needed, loading all items when filtering for one\n\n## Phase 3: Fix Issues\n\nWait for all three agents to complete. Aggregate their findings and fix each issue directly. If a finding is a false positive or not worth addressing, note it and move on — do not argue with the finding, just skip it.\n\nWhen done, briefly summarize what was fixed (or confirm the code was already clean).\n\n\n## Additional Focus\n\nunwanted.py"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a7304902-9a50-42b0-92ed-a02d847b427f","uuid":"880e222d-70ee-49e1-b540-be2f79c549e7","isSynthetic":true}
